باب كفالة الرجلين
ترجمہ یہ باب دو شخصوں کی کفالت کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح جب فاضل مصنف ایک شخص کے کفالہ کے ذکر سے فارغ ہو گئے تو اب دو شخصوں کے کفالہ کو ذکر فرما رہے ہیں ۔ اور دو چونکہ طبعاً ایک کے بعد ہوتے ہیں اسلئے وضعا بھی اس کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا تا کہ وضع طبع کے مناسب ہو جائے۔ یوں بھی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ ایک شخص کی کفالت بمنزلہ مفرد کے ہے اور دو کی کفالت بمنزلہ مرکب کے ہے اور مفرد، مرکب سے مقدم ہوتا ہے اسلئے کفالہ واحد کو پہلے اور کفالہ اثنین کو بعد میں ذکر فر مایا۔ دو آدمیوں پر قرض ہو اور ہر ایک دوسرے کا کفیل ہو تو ادا ئیگی کی صورت میں دوسرے پر رجوع کرے گا یا نہیں
واذا كان الدين على اثنين وكل واحد منهما كفيل عن صاحبه كما اذا اشتريا عبداً بالف درهم وكفل كل واحد منهما عن صاحبه فما ادى احدهما لم يرجع على شريكه حتى يزيد ما يؤديه على النصف فيرجع بالزيادة لان كل واحد منهما في النصف اصيل وفى النصف الأخر كفيل ولا معارضة بين ما عليه بحق الاصالة وبحق الكفالة لان الاول دين والثانى مطالبة ثم هو تابع للاول فيقع عن الأول وفى الزيادة لامعارضة فيقع عن الكفالة ولانه لو وقع فى النصف عن صاحبه فيرجع عليه فلصاحبه ان يرجع لان ادا نائبه كا دائه فيودى إلى الدور
ترجمہ اگر قرضہ دو شخصوں پر ہو اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی طرف سے کفیل ہے مثلاً دو آدمیوں نے ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض ایک غلام خریدا۔ اور دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی طرف سے کفیل ہو گیا تو اُن دونوں میں سے جس نے جو کچھ ادا کیا وہ اپنے شریک سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ یہاں تک کہ جو کچھ وہ ادا کرے گا اگر نصف سے بڑھ جائے تو وہ زائد کو واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک، ایک نصف میں اصیل اور دوسرے نصف میں کفیل ہے اور اس پر جو نصف بحق اصالت ہے اور جو بحق کفالت ہے۔ ان دونوں میں کوئی معارضہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اول دین ہے اور ثانی مطالبہ ہے۔ پھر ثانی اول کے تابع ہے تو ادا کیا ہوا اول سے واقع ہوگا۔ اور نصف سے زائد میں بھی کوئی معاوضہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نصف سے زائد کفالہ سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور اس لئے کہ اگر نصف میں اس کے ساتھی کی طرف سے واقع ہو اور وہ اُس سے واپس لے تو اس کے ساتھی کو بھی واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کے نائب کا ادا کرنا اس کے ادا کرنے کے مانند ہے لہذا یہ دور کا سبب ہوگا۔
Chapter of Guarantee of Two Persons. Translation: This chapter is about the guarantee of two persons. Explanation: When the author finished mentioning the guarantee of one person, he now mentions the guarantee of two persons. And since two naturally come after one, he arranged it accordingly. It can also be said that one person's guarantee is like a simple term, and two persons' guarantee is like a compound term, so the simple precedes the compound. Ruling when two persons owe a debt and each is a guarantor for the other: And if the debt is upon two, and each one of them is a guarantor for his companion, as when they buy a slave for one thousand dirhams and each guarantees for his companion, then whichever of them pays, he does not have recourse against his partner until what he pays exceeds half; then he has recourse for the excess. Because each one of them is principal in half and guarantor in the other half. There is no conflict between what is upon him by right of principalship and by right of guarantee, because the first is a debt and the second a claim. Then the second is subordinate to the first, so the payment falls upon the first. And in the excess there is no conflict, so it falls upon the guarantee. And because if it fell upon the half for his companion and he had recourse against him, then the companion would also have the right to recourse, because the payment of his deputy is like his own payment, leading to circularity.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on kafālah involving two persons (kafālat al-rajulayn). The author explains the order: just as a simple term precedes a compound, so the guarantee of one person is discussed before that of two. The core ruling is a detailed case: two persons jointly purchase a slave for 1000 dirhams, and each stands as guarantor for the other. The question is: if one pays back the debt, can he recover from his partner? The answer is that he can only recover the amount exceeding half of the debt. The reasoning is that each debtor is a principal (aṣīl) for half of the debt and a guarantor (kafīl) for the other half. When he pays, the payment first applies to his own principal portion (the half he owes as principal), and only the excess over half is considered paid on behalf of his partner as guarantor. This avoids circularity (dawr): if the payment were attributed to the partner's half, the partner could also claim back from the payer, leading to an endless cycle. Therefore, the excess is recoverable, but no more.

Key Terms
أصيل (aṣīl): Principal debtor; the one who is primarily liable for the debt.
كفيل (kafīl): Guarantor; one who undertakes to pay the debt of another.
دور (dawr): Circularity; logical impossibility where each party's claim relies on the other's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 4000 dirhams
B) 2000 dirhams
C) 6000 dirhams
D) 0 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In mutual guarantee, each debtor is principal for half, so only the excess over half is recoverable from the partner.

Ruling on Recourse in Joint Guarantee Between Co-Guarantors
Legal ruling with two proofs on recovery between co-guarantors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a co-guarantor can recover from his partner, and explain both proofs (strength comparison and infinite regress) that justify the ruling.

Core Idea
A paying partner can only recover from his co-guarantor the amount paid beyond his own share of the debt.

Imagine two people jointly borrow 1,000 dirhams, each guaranteeing the other. If one pays 600, how much can he get back from his partner? The Hanafi school gives a precise answer: only the excess over half. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this seemingly simple rule, exploring concepts like the strength of principal debt versus guarantee, and the logical problem of infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Restate the case: two partners jointly borrow 1,000 dirhams, each is guarantor for the other. One partner pays an amount. The ruling: if payment ≤ 500, no recourse; if > 500, recover the excess.
2
Analyze the first proof: strength of liability
Each partner is principal (asīl) for 500 dirhams (his own debt) and guarantor (kafīl) for the other 500. The debt owed as principal is stronger (aqwā) than the mere claim (mutālabah) owed as guarantor. Up to 500, any payment is attributed to the stronger principal liability, so the payer is just paying his own debt and cannot reclaim. Beyond 500, there is no principal liability, so payment is attributed to guarantee, allowing recourse.
Key maxim: al-tābi' tābi' (the subordinate follows the principal).
3
Analyze the second proof: infinite regress
If recourse were allowed for exactly half (500), each partner could argue agency (niyābah) to reclaim the amount indefinitely, creating a never-ending cycle (tasalsul). Since tasalsul is invalid (bātil), recourse for half is invalid. For amounts beyond half, the regress breaks because after paying his own share, the first partner ceases to be a guarantor for the other.
The text also discusses the indivisible part (juz' lā yatajzza') to show that any partial payment can be split further, reinforcing regress.
4
Apply the ruling to a new example
Given a payment of 700 dirhams, the first 500 are attributed to principal (no recourse), the remaining 200 are as guarantor, so the payer can recover 200 from his partner.
Verifying understanding.

Source Text

دلیل یہ ہے کہ شریکین میں سے ہر ایک نصف در اہم یعنی پانچ سو دراہم میں تو اصیل ہے اور نصف یعنی دوسرے پانچ سو میں کفیل ہے۔ یعنی شریکین میں ہر ایک پر پانچ سو درہم بحق کفالت واجب ہیں۔ اور جو دراہم بحق اصالت واجب ہیں وہ تو قرضہ ہیں اور جو بحق کفالت واجب ہیں ان کا فقط مطالبہ واجب ہے کفیل پر ڈین واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ مطالبہ دین کے مقابلہ میں دین اقویٰ ہوتا ہے۔ نیز مطالبہ دین ، دین کے تابع ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مطالبہ دین بغیر دین کے ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پس کفالہ یعنی مطالبہ دین تابع ہوا اور اصالت یعنی دین متبوع ہوا۔ اور متبوع بہ نسبت تابع کے اقوامی ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے جو دراہم بحق اصالت واجب ہیں یعنی قرضہ ہیں وہ اقوی ہیں اور جو بحق کفالت واجب ہیں یعنی فقط مطالبہ دین ہے وہ اضعف میں اتوی مرا ضعف کے درمیان حقیقتا کوئی معارضہ نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ معارضہ کے لئے دونوں جانب کا قوت وضعف میں برابر ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ ما علیہ بحق الاصالۃ اور ماعلیہ بحق الکفالہ کے درمیان کوئی معارضہ نہیں ہے۔ اور جب ماعلیہ بحق الا صالہ اور ماعلی الکفالہ کے درمیان کوئی معارضہ نہیں ہے تو شریکین میں سے ایک، نصف یعنی پانچ سو تک جو در ہم ادا کرے گا ان کو اقومی یعنی ما علیہ بحق الا صالہ کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس نے وہ دراہم ادا کئے ہیں جو اس پر قرضہ ہیں۔ اور جب اس نے اپنا قرضہ ادا کیا ہے تو اس کو اپنے شریک سے واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ادائیگی میں ماعلیہ بحق الاصالة یعنی قرضہ کو ماعلیہ بق الکفالہ پر ترجیح ہوگی اور پانچ سو تک قرضہ کی ادائیگی شمار ہوگی نہ کہ ماعلیہ بحق الکفالہ کی ادائیگی ۔ اور پانچ سو سے زائد میں من کل وجہ کوئی معارضہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ پانچ سو سے زائد اس پر بحق اصالت واجب نہیں ہیں ۔ بلکہ پانچ سو سے زائد بحق کفالت واجب ہیں۔ اور جب پانچ سو سے زائد حق کفالت واجب ہیں تو پانچ سو زائد جو مقدار ادا کرے گاوہ بحق کفالت شمار ہوگی ۔ یعنی یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس نے کفیل ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ مقدار زائدا اپنے شریک کی طرف سے ادا کی ہے اور کفیل جب مکفول عنہ، کی طرف سے مال ادا کر دے تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے بشرطیکہ مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے تھیل ہوا ہو ۔ اس لئے اس مسئلہ میں ادا کرنے والے شریک کو یہ اختیار ہوگا کہ وہ پانچ سو سے زائد اپنے دوسرے شریک سے واپس لے لے۔
دوسری دلیل سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین فرما لیجئے کہ عبارت میں دور سے حقیقتہ دور مراد نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تسلسل مراد ہے اور تسلسل لائی نہا یہ باطل ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ جز لا تجری باطل ہے یعنی ایسا کوئی جز نہیں ہے جس کی تقسیم اور تجری نہ ہو سکتی ہو۔ اب اس دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ احد الشریکین کو نصف دین ادا کرنے کی صورت میں آخر سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار اس وجہ سے نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ رجوع کا اختیار دینے کی صورت میں تسلسل لازم آتا ہے بایں طور کہ نصف دین ادا کرنے والا اپنے شریک سے کہے گا کہ یہ نصف دین میں نے بحیثیت کفیل کے تیری جانب سے ادا کیا ہے۔ لہذا تم واپس کر و۔ پس شریک آخر ادا کرنے والے کو نصف دین واپس کرے گا۔ اب شریک آخر کہے گا کہ تم دین ادا کرنے میں میرے نائب تھے۔ اور نائب کا ادا کرنا در حقیقت اصل کا ادا کرنا ہے۔ لہذا تیرا ادا کرنا در حقیقت میرا ادا کرنا ہوا اور اگر شریک آخر ادا کرتا تو اس کو کفیل ہونے کی وجہ سے شریک اوّل سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی شریک آخر کو شریک اوّل سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ لہذا شریک آخر ، شریک اوّل سے نصف دین واپس لے گا۔ اب شریک اوّل شریک آخر سے کہے گا کہ تو نے میرا نا ئب ہو کر ادا کیا ہے اور نائب کا ادا کرنا اصل کا ادا کرنا ہے۔ لہذا تیرا ادا کرنا در حقیقت میرا ادا کرنا ہوا۔ اور جب میں نے ادا کیا ہے اور میں تیرا کفیل ہوں تو ، تو اس کو واپس کر ۔ پس شریک آخر شریک اوّل کو واپس کرے گا۔ پھر شریک آخر ، شریک اول سے یہی تقریر کر کے واپس لے گا۔ پھر شریک اول یہی تقریر کر کے شریک آخر سے واپس لے گا۔ اور یہ سلسلہ قیامت تک چلتا رہے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ نصف دین ادا کرنے کی صورت میں اگر ادا کرنے والے کو رجوع کا اختیار دیا جائے تو تسلسل لازم آتا ہے۔ اور تسلسل باطل ہے اور جو چیز باطل کوستلزم ہو وہ چونکہ خود باطل ہوتی ہے اس لئے نصف دین ادا کرنے کی صورت میں اپنے شریک سے رجوع کرنا باطل ہے اور نصف دین سے زائد ادا کرنے کی صورت میں مقدار زائد اپنے شریک سے واپس لینے میں کوئی تسلسل لازم نہیں آتا۔ مثلا ایک شریک نے چھ سو درہم ادا کئے ۔ پانچ سو درہم اصیل ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور ایک سو درہم کفیل ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور ایک سو درہم اپنے شریک سے واپس لے لئے تو اب اس کو شریک اول سے واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اب شریک آخر یہ نہیں کہہ سکتا کہ یہ ایک سو درہم تو نے میرا نا ئب ہو کر ادا کئے ہیں اور نائب کا ادا کرنا اصل کا ادا کرنا ہے۔ لہذا تیرا ادا کرنا در حقیقت میرا ادا کرنا ہے۔ اور میں بھی کفیل ہوں لہذا ایک سو درہم مجھ کو واپس کر ۔ اور یہ اس لئے نہیں کہہ سکتا کہ جب شریک اول بحیثیت اصیل کے پانچ سو درہم ادا کر چکا تو شریک آخر ، شریک اول کا کفیل نہ رہا۔ اور جب شریک آخر ،شریک اول کا کفیل نہ رہا تو شریک آخر کو شریک اول سے رجوع کا اختیار بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب رجوع کا اختیار نہیں ہے تو تسلسل بھی لازم نہ آئے گا۔ اور جب تسلسل لازم نہیں آیا تو شریک اول کو شریک آخر سے مقدا بر زائد یعنی ایک سو درہم رجوع کرنے کا اختیار بھی حاصل ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کی یہ تقریر، استاذ مکرم حضرت مولانامحمد حسین صاحب بہاری مدظلہ، کے بیان کے مطابق ہے جو درست ہے۔ لیکن صاحب فتح القدیر نے اس دلیل کی تقریر اس طرح کی ہے کہ اگر ایک شریک نے مثلاً دوسو درہم ادا کئے تو وہ ایک سو درہم ادا کرنے میں اصیل ہوا اور ایک سو میں کفیل ہوا۔ یعنی ایک سو درہم بحق اصالت ادا کئے اور ایک سو درہم بحق کفالت ادا کئے پس وہ دوسرے شریک سے وہ ایک سو درہم واپس لے گا جو اس نے بحق کفالہ ادا کئے ہیں۔ پھر دوسرا شریک ایک سو درہم شریک اول کو واپس دے کر یہ کہے گا کہ تو نے ایک سو درہم میرا نا ئب ہو کر ادا کئے ہیں۔ اور نائب کا ادا کرنا اصل کا ادا کرنا ہے۔ لہذا تیرا ادا کرنا در حقیقت میرا ادا کرنا ہے۔ گویا دوسرے شریک نے ایک سو درہم ادا کئے ہیں۔ ان میں سے پچاس حق اصالہ ہوں گے اور پچاس بحق کفالہ ہوں گے۔ پس دوسرا شریک وہ پچاس درہم جو بحق کفالہ ادا کئے ہیں ان کو شریک اوّل سے واپس لیگا۔ پھر شریک اول کہے گا کہ پچاس درہم جو تو نے میری طرف سے ادا کئے ہیں میرا نا ئب ہو کر ادا کئے ہیں اور نائب کا ادا کرنا اصل کا ادا کرنا ہے۔ لہذا تیرا ادا کرنا در حقیقت میرا ادا کرنا ہے اور جب میں نے ادا کئے ہیں تو ان میں نصف یعنی پچیس درہم بحق اصالۃ ہوں گے اور نصف یعنی چھپیں بحق کفالت ہوں گے۔ لہذا وہ پچیس درہم جو میں نے بحق کفالہ ادا کئے ہیں ان کو واپس کرو۔ پھر دوسرا شریک چھپیں درہم واپس کرنے کے بعد یہی تقریر کرے گا۔ اور جزلا تجری چونکہ باطل ہے اس لئے یہ سلسلہ الی نہا یہ چلتا رہے گا۔ اور تسلسل لازم آئے گا۔ اور تسلسل باطل ہے۔ لہذا نصف دین تک اپنے ساتھی سے رجوع کرنا بھی باطل ہے۔ اور نصف دین سے زائد میں چونکہ
Two men jointly borrowed one thousand dirhams, and each of them became a guarantor (kafeel) for his partner. Then, if one of them pays some amount, he will not have the right to recover it from his partner. But if the paid amount exceeds half, then he can recover the excess amount from his partner. For example, if one partner paid six hundred dirhams to the seller or creditor, then he can recover one hundred dirhams from his other partner.
The proof is that each of the two partners is a principal (aseel) in half (i.e., five hundred dirhams) and a guarantor in the other half (i.e., the other five hundred). That is, each partner is liable for five hundred dirhams by way of guarantee (kafalah). And there is no real conflict between the dirhams that are owed by way of principality (asālah) and those owed by way of guarantee (kafālah), because the dirhams owed by way of principality are stronger (aqwā), while those owed by way of guarantee are weaker (ad'af) in comparison. This is because what is owed by way of principality is a debt (dayn), whereas what is owed by way of guarantee is only a claim (mutālabah); the guarantor does not owe the debt. And it is accepted that the debt is stronger than the claim for the debt. Also, the claim for the debt is subordinate (tābi') to the debt, because the claim for the debt is not possible without the debt. Thus, kafālah (i.e., the claim for the debt) is subordinate, and asālah (i.e., the debt) is the principal (matbū'). And the principal is stronger than the subordinate. Therefore, the dirhams owed by way of principality (i.e., the debt) are strong, and those owed by way of guarantee (i.e., only a claim) are weak, and between strong and weak there is no real conflict, because conflict requires both sides to be equal in strength and weakness. So it is established that there is no conflict between what is owed by way of principality and what is owed by way of guarantee. And when there is no conflict, if one of the partners pays up to half (i.e., five hundred dirhams), those dirhams will be attributed to the stronger (i.e., what is owed by way of principality). And it will be said that he paid those dirhams which were his debt. And when he has paid his debt, he will not have the right to recover from his partner. The result is that in payment, what is owed by way of principality (the debt) takes precedence over what is owed by way of guarantee, and up to five hundred, it will be counted as payment of the debt, not as payment of what is owed by way of guarantee. And beyond five hundred, there is no conflict from any perspective, because beyond five hundred he is not liable by way of principality. Rather, beyond five hundred is owed by way of guarantee. And when beyond five hundred is owed by way of guarantee, whatever amount he pays beyond five hundred will be counted as payment by way of guarantee. That is, it will be said that he paid this excess amount from his partner's side because he is a guarantor. And when a guarantor pays property on behalf of the principal (makfūl 'anhu), the guarantor has the right to recover from the principal, provided that he paid with the principal's consent. Therefore, in this issue, the paying partner will have the right to recover the excess beyond five hundred from his other partner.
Before the second proof, please note that in the phrase [the text mentions 'dawr' (circularity) but] not actual circularity is meant; rather, infinite regress (tasalsul) is meant, and infinite regress is invalid. The second point is that the indivisible part (juz' lā yatajzza') is invalid, meaning there is no part that cannot be divided and split. Now the summary of this proof is that when one of the two partners pays half the debt, he will not be given the right to recourse from the other because giving the right to recourse leads to infinite regress. This is because the one who paid half the debt will say to his partner: 'I have paid this half debt as a guarantor on your behalf, so return it.' Then the other partner will return half the debt to the paying partner. Now the other partner will say: 'You were my agent (nā'ib) in paying the debt, and the agent's payment is effectively the principal's payment. So your payment is effectively my payment. And if the other partner had paid, he would have the right to recourse from the first partner because he is a guarantor. So in this case too, the other partner has the right to recourse from the first partner. Therefore, the other partner will take back half the debt from the first partner. Now the first partner will say to the other partner: 'You paid as my agent, and the agent's payment is effectively the principal's payment. So your payment is effectively my payment. And when I have paid, and I am your guarantor, then you return it.' So the other partner will return it to the first partner. Then the other partner will take it back from the first partner using the same argument. Then the first partner will take it back from the other partner using the same argument. And this series will continue until the Day of Judgment. The result is that if the payer is given the right to recourse when paying half the debt, then infinite regress becomes necessary. And infinite regress is invalid, and whatever necessitates the invalid is itself invalid. Therefore, in the case of paying half the debt, recourse from one's partner is invalid. And in the case of paying more than half, there is no infinite regress in the excess amount. For example, one partner paid six hundred dirhams: five hundred dirhams as a principal and one hundred dirhams as a guarantor. And he recovered one hundred dirhams from his partner. Then the other partner will not have the right to recourse from the first partner. Because now the other partner cannot say: 'You paid these one hundred dirhams as my agent, and the agent's payment is effectively the principal's payment. So your payment is effectively my payment. And I am also a guarantor, so return the hundred dirhams to me.' And he cannot say this because when the first partner has already paid five hundred dirhams as a principal, the other partner ceased to be the first partner's guarantor. And when the other partner is no longer the first partner's guarantor, the other partner has no right to recourse from the first partner. And when there is no right to recourse, infinite regress does not become necessary. And when infinite regress does not become necessary, the first partner has the right to recover from the other partner the excess amount, i.e., one hundred dirhams. This presentation of the proof is according to the explanation of our respected teacher, Mawlana Muhammad Husain Sahib Bahari (may his shadow be prolonged), which is correct. However, the author of Fath al-Qadir presented this proof as follows: If one partner paid, for example, two hundred dirhams, then he was a principal in paying one hundred dirhams and a guarantor in one hundred dirhams. That is, he paid one hundred dirhams by way of principality and one hundred dirhams by way of guarantee. So he will recover from the other partner that one hundred dirhams which he paid by way of guarantee. Then the other partner, after returning one hundred dirhams to the first partner, will say: 'You paid one hundred dirhams as my agent, and the agent's payment is effectively the principal's payment. So your payment is effectively my payment.' It is as if the other partner paid one hundred dirhams. Out of that, fifty will be by way of principality and fifty by way of guarantee. So the other partner will recover from the first partner the fifty dirhams that he paid by way of guarantee. Then the first partner will say: 'The fifty dirhams that you paid on my behalf were paid as my agent, and the agent's payment is effectively the principal's payment. So your payment is effectively my payment. And when I have paid, out of them, half, i.e., twenty-five dirhams, will be by way of principality, and half, i.e., twenty-five dirhams, will be by way of guarantee. Therefore, return those twenty-five dirhams that I paid by way of guarantee.' Then the other partner, after returning twenty-five dirhams, will make the same argument. And since the indivisible part is invalid, this series will continue endlessly. And infinite regress becomes necessary. And infinite regress is invalid. Therefore, recourse from one's partner up to half the debt is also invalid. And beyond half, since...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah (a commentary on al-Hidayah) presents a specific ruling in the Hanafi law of suretyship (kafalah). The scenario involves two individuals who jointly borrow 1,000 dirhams, each simultaneously becoming a guarantor for the other. The ruling: if one partner makes a payment of 500 dirhams or less, he cannot recover anything from his co-guarantor. If he pays more than 500 dirhams (e.g., 600), he can recover the excess (100) from his partner.

The first proof uses a comparison of legal strength. Each partner is a principal (asīl) regarding 500 dirhams (his own debt) and a guarantor (kafīl) regarding the other 500. The debt (dayn) owed by virtue of being a principal is stronger (aqwā) than the mere claim (mutālabah) that arises from being a guarantor. Since the debtor cannot reclaim his own debt payment, amounts up to 500 are attributed to his principal liability, blocking recourse. Beyond 500, no principal liability exists, so the payment is attributed to guarantee, allowing recourse.

The second proof is a reductio ad absurdum using the concept of infinite regress (tasalsul). If recourse were allowed for exactly half the debt, each partner could argue agency (niyābah) to reclaim the amount indefinitely, creating a never-ending cycle. Since infinite regress is invalid (bātil), recourse for half is invalid. For amounts beyond half, the cycle breaks because after paying his own 500 share, the first partner ceases to be a guarantor for the other, preventing the regress. The text also discusses a variant presentation by the author of Fath al-Qadir, which further illustrates the regress using the indivisibility of parts (juz' lā yatajzza').

Key Terms
كفالة (kafālah): Suretyship; a contract where one person (kafīl) becomes responsible for a debt or obligation of another (makfūl 'anhu) to a creditor (makfūl lahu). In this passage, each partner is kafīl for the other.
أصالة (asālah): Principality; being the original debtor. In this passage, each partner is asīl (principal) for half the debt.
مطالبة (mutālabah): Claim; the right to demand payment. In kafālah, the guarantor is subject only to a claim for payment, not the debt itself.
تابع (tābi'): Subordinate; the claim for the debt is subordinate (tābi') to the debt itself, as it cannot exist without the debt.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Infinite regress; an endless chain of reasoning or actions. In this passage, allowing recourse for half the debt leads to an infinite cycle of claims.
جز لا يتجزى (juz' lā yatajzza'): Indivisible part; the concept that some things cannot be further divided. In this passage, it is declared invalid, meaning every amount can be halved indefinitely, leading to infinite regress.

Two partners jointly borrow 1000 dirhams, each guaranteeing the other. One partner pays 600 dirhams. How much can he recover from the other partner?
A) 500 dirhams
B) 100 dirhams
C) 300 dirhams
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In a joint guarantee where each partner is both principal and surety, payment up to half is attributed to one's own debt (no recourse), and any excess is recoverable from the co-guarantor.

Ruling on Recourse When a Co-Guarantor Pays Half or More of a Joint Debt
Explaining why paying half leads to infinite regress and invalidates recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a co-guarantor's recourse after paying half or more than half of a joint debt and explain why paying half leads to infinite regress (tasalsul).

Core Idea
Paying exactly half of a joint debt as a co-guarantor invalidates recourse due to infinite regress; paying more than half allows recovery of the excess.

In Hanafi fiqh, when two partners are also mutual guarantors for a joint debt, the amount paid by one affects the validity of recourse against the other. This passage from a commentary on al-Hidayah uses rational proof (dalil aqli) based on infinite regress (tasalsul) to distinguish between paying half and paying more than half. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the rules of kafalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two partners are each other's guarantors for a joint debt. One partner pays part of the debt toward the creditor. The issue is whether he can recover from his partner.
The partners are both principals and guarantors simultaneously.
2
State the general Hanafi ruling
If he pays exactly half, recourse to his partner is invalid (batil). If he pays more than half, he may recover the excess amount.
The boundary is the half amount of the total joint debt.
3
Understand the proof (dalil aqli) for the half case
The passage uses infinite regress: if recourse were allowed for half, each partner could argue the payment was as deputy, leading to an endless cycle of claims and counter-claims.
Infinite regress (tasalsul) is considered rationally invalid.
4
Examine the two explanations
One explanation (from a teacher) shows the regress via the 'deputy' argument; another (from Fath al-Qadir) uses halving fractions. Both conclude tasalsul is batil, so recourse is invalid.
The two explanations are different presentations of the same rational proof.
5
Apply to more than half
Paying more than half breaks the symmetry; the excess is recovered because the payer acted as a guarantor for that excess, and no regress occurs.
The paying partner's own share as principal is fully covered, leaving a clear guarantor portion.

اصالۃ ہوں گے اور نصف یعنی چھپیں بحق کفالت ہوں گے۔ لہذا وہ پچیس درہم جو میں نے بحق کفالہ ادا کئے ہیں ان کو واپس کرو۔ پھر دوسرا شریک چھپیں درہم واپس کرنے کے بعد یہی تقریر کرے گا۔ اور جزلا تجری چونکہ باطل ہے اس لئے یہ سلسلہ الی نہا یہ چلتا رہے گا۔ اور تسلسل لازم آئے گا۔ اور تسلسل باطل ہے۔ لہذا نصف دین تک اپنے ساتھی سے رجوع کرنا بھی باطل ہے۔ اور نصف دین سے زائد میں چونکہ تسلسل لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے نصف دین سے زائد کور جوع کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
The other partner will say: 'You were my deputy in paying the debt. And the deputy's payment is in reality the principal's payment. Therefore your payment is in reality my payment.' And if the other partner pays, he would have the right to recourse to the first partner on the basis of being a guarantor. So in this case also, the other partner has the right to recourse to the first partner. Hence the other partner will take back half the debt from the first partner. Now the first partner will say to the other partner: 'You paid as my deputy, and the deputy's payment is the principal's payment. Therefore your payment is in reality my payment. And since I have paid, and I am your guarantor, you must return it to me.' So the other partner will return it to the first partner. Then the other partner will make the same argument and take it back from the first partner. Then the first partner will make the same argument and take it back from the other partner. And this cycle will continue until the Day of Judgment. The conclusion is that in the case of paying half the debt, if the payer is given the right of recourse, an infinite regress necessarily arises. And infinite regress is invalid. And whatever leads to something invalid is itself invalid. Therefore, in the case of paying half the debt, recourse to one's partner is invalid. And in the case of paying more than half, there is no infinite regress in taking back the excess from the partner. For example, one partner paid six hundred dirhams: five hundred dirhams as a principal and one hundred dirhams as a guarantor, and he took back one hundred dirhams from his partner. Then he will not have the right to recourse to the first partner. Because now the other partner cannot say: 'You paid these one hundred dirhams as my deputy, and the deputy's payment is the principal's payment. Therefore your payment is in reality my payment. And I am also a guarantor, so return the one hundred dirhams to me.' And he cannot say this because when the first partner paid five hundred dirhams as a principal, the other partner ceased to be his guarantor. And when the other partner is no longer his guarantor, he has no right of recourse to the first partner. And when there is no right of recourse, no infinite regress occurs. And when infinite regress does not occur, the first partner has the right to recourse to the other partner for the excess amount, i.e., one hundred dirhams. This presentation of the proof is according to the explanation of our respected teacher Maulana Muhammad Hussain Sahib Bahari, may his shade be prolonged, which is correct. But the author of Fath al-Qadir has presented the proof in this way: If one partner paid, for example, two hundred dirhams, then he is a principal in paying one hundred dirhams and a guarantor in paying one hundred dirhams. That is, he paid one hundred dirhams as a principal and one hundred dirhams as a guarantor. So he will take back from the other partner those one hundred dirhams which he paid as a guarantor. Then the other partner will return one hundred dirhams to the first partner and say: 'You paid one hundred dirhams as my deputy, and the deputy's payment is the principal's payment. Therefore your payment is in reality my payment.' Thus it is as if the second partner paid one hundred dirhams. From that, fifty will be as a principal and fifty as a guarantor. So the second partner will take back from the first partner those fifty dirhams which he paid as a guarantor. Then the first partner will say: 'The fifty dirhams which you paid on my behalf, you paid as my deputy, and the deputy's payment is the principal's payment. Therefore your payment is in reality my payment. And since I have paid, from those, half (twenty-five dirhams) will be as a principal and half (twenty-five) as a guarantor. So return those twenty-five dirhams which I paid as a guarantor.' Then the second partner will make the same argument after returning twenty-five dirhams. And since infinite division is invalid, this cycle will continue indefinitely, and infinite regress will occur. And infinite regress is invalid. Therefore, recourse to one's partner up to half the debt is also invalid. And in the case of more than half, since infinite regress does not occur, there is no harm in recourse for the excess beyond half.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in suretyship (kafalah) where two partners are also each other's guarantors for a joint debt. The text examines the legal ruling on whether one partner can recover from the other after paying the debt. The key issue is the possibility of infinite regress (tasalsul) if only half the debt is paid, because each partner could argue that the payment was made as a deputy (na'ib), leading to a never-ending cycle. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between paying exactly half and paying more than half. If only half is paid, recourse is invalid because it leads to infinite regress, which is logically impossible (batil). If more than half is paid, there is no such problem, and the excess can be recovered. The text provides two explanations: one from a teacher and one from Fath al-Qadir, both reaching the same conclusion. The practical implication is that co-guarantors must be careful about the amount paid to avoid the infinite regress issue. The Hanafi position is based on rational proof (dalil aqli) using the principle that whatever leads to something invalid is itself invalid.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of suretyship where one person (kafeel) guarantees the debt or obligation of another (asil) to a third party (makful lahu).
نائب (na'ib): A deputy or representative who acts on behalf of another; in this context, a co-guarantor who pays the debt is considered a deputy of the other co-guarantor.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Infinite regress; an endless chain of events or arguments that is logically impossible.
باطل (batil): Legally invalid or void; an act that has no legal effect and must be repeated if it is an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling, what is the consequence if a co-guarantor pays exactly half of a joint debt and then seeks recourse from the other co-guarantor?
A) Recourse is valid because the paying partner is a guarantor.
B) Recourse is invalid because it leads to infinite regress.
C) Recourse is valid only if the other partner agrees.
D) Recourse is invalid because the debt is considered paid by both equally.

Key Takeaway
A co-guarantor who pays exactly half of a joint debt cannot recover that half from the other guarantor due to infinite regress; if he pays more than half, the excess is recoverable.

Two Guarantors with Mutual Suretyship: Recourse for Half the Amount
Stating the ruling that each guarantor can recover half from the other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recourse between co-guarantors with mutual suretyship and explain why it does not lead to a vicious cycle.

Core Idea
Each co-guarantor can recover half from the other; equality prevents a cycle.

When two people guarantee a debt jointly and also guarantee each other, a question arises: can the one who pays recover from the other? This lesson walks through the Hanafi ruling, its logical basis, and why it avoids the pitfall of infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two guarantors (kafeel) for a principal debtor (asil), with the additional condition that each is also a guarantor for the other.
2
State the ruling
Each guarantor who pays the debt can recover half of what he paid from his co-guarantor, regardless of the amount.
The half is of what was paid, not of the total debt.
3
Examine the reasoning
The guarantee is for the entire amount from both sides; the payment is jointly attributed, so no part has preference.
The combination of guarantees makes the payment shared equally.
4
Address the cycle objection
This does not create a vicious cycle (dawr) because equality is achieved by the half recovery; the resulting balance is stable.
In previous cases without mutual guarantee, a cycle could occur.
5
Recognize the analogy
The validity of guaranteeing a guarantor is analogically derived from the validity of guaranteeing the principal and from hawala (debt transfer).
Qiyas confirms that the mutual guarantee is valid.

احدهما رجع على صاحبه بنصفه قليلاً كان أو كثيراً ومعنى المسألة في الصحيح ان يكون الكفالة بالكل عن الاصيل وبالكل عن الشريك والمطالبة متعددة فيجتمع الكفالتان على مامرو موجبها التزام المطالبة فتصح الكفالة الى الدورلان قضيته الاستواء وقد حصل برجوع احدهما بنصف ما ادى فلاينقض برجوع الاخر عليه بخلاف ما تقدم ثم يرجعان على الاصيل لانهما اديا عنه احدهما بنفسه والآخر بنائبه وان شاء رجع بالجميع على المكفول عنه مطالبہ متعدد ہے۔ پس دو کفالے جمع ہو جائیں گے جیسا کہ گذر چکا ہے۔ اور کفالہ کا موجب مطالبہ کو لازم کرنا ہے۔ پس کفیل کی طرف سے بھی کفیل ہو نا صحیح ہے جیسا کہ اصیل کی طرف سے کفیل ہونا صحیح ہے اور جیسے محتال علیہ کی طرف سے حوالہ کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اور جب یہ معلوم ہو چکا تو ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے جو کچھ ادا کیا وہ اُن دونوں کی طرف سے مشترکہ طور پر واقع ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ کل کا کل کفالہ ہے۔ لہذا بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح نہ ہوگی ۔ بر خلاف ما تقدم کے ۔ پس وہ اپنے شریک سے نصف واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ اور دور کا سبب بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا مقتضی برابری ہے۔ اور برابری ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے مالڈی کا نصف رجوع کرنے سے حاصل ہو گئی تو اُس پر دوسرے کے رجوع کرنے سے برابری نہیں توڑی جائے گی برخلاف ما تقدم کے۔ پھر یہ دونوں کفیل اپنے اصیل سے واپس لے سکتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ ایک نے اصیل کی طرف سے بذات خود ادا کیا ہے اور دوسرے نے اپنے نائب کے ذریعہ ادا کیا ہے۔ اور اگر چاہے ادا کئے ہوئے پورے مال کو مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے ۔ کیونکہ وہ مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے اس کے حکم سے پورے مال کا کفیل ہوا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو شخص ایک آدمی کی طرف سے اس شرط پر مال کے کفیل ہو گئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہرا ایک دوسرے کی طرف سے بھی کفیل ہے۔ پس دونوں کفیلوں میں سے ایک نے جو کچھ ادا کیا ہو وہ اپنے ساتھی سے اس کا نصف واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے۔ ادا کی ہوئی رقم خواہ قلیل ہو خواہ کثیر ہو ۔ مثلا حامد اور خالد شاہد کی طرف سے دوسو درہم کے اس شرط پر کفیل ہو گئے کہ حامد ، خالد کی طرف سے
Two men become guarantors for a man regarding property, on the condition that each of them is a guarantor for his companion. Will they have recourse against each other in the event of payment? (Arabic text: And if two men become guarantors for a man regarding property on the condition that each of them is a guarantor for his companion, then everything that one of them pays, he can recover half from his companion, whether it is little or much. The meaning of the issue in the correct view is that the guarantee is for the entire amount from the principal and for the entire amount from the companion, and the demand is multiple. So the two guarantees combine as previously, and the consequence of guarantee is the obligation to meet the demand. So becoming a guarantor for a guarantor is valid just as becoming a guarantor for the principal is valid, and just as hawala (transfer of debt) from the person against whom it is transferred is valid. Once this is known, whatever one of them pays is jointly attributed to both, because each has a guarantee for the whole. So no part has preference over any other, contrary to what preceded. Thus he can recover half from his companion, and it does not lead to a cycle, because its requirement is equality, and equality is achieved by one of them recovering half of what he paid, so it is not broken by the other's recourse against him, contrary to what preceded. Then both can have recourse against the principal, because one paid directly and the other through his deputy. And if he wishes, he can have recourse for the entire amount against the person guaranteed, because he guaranteed the entire amount at his command. Explanation: The scenario of the issue is that two persons become guarantors for one man on the condition that each of them is also a guarantor for the other. So whatever one of them pays, he is authorized to recover half from his companion, whether the amount paid is little or much. For example, Hamid and Khalid become guarantors for Shahid for two hundred dirhams on the condition that Hamid is from Khalid's side...
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents a distinct ruling in kafalah: when two people act as guarantors for a third, with the additional stipulation that each is also a guarantor for the other, the Hanafi ruling is that each can recover half of whatever he pays from his co-guarantor. This is because the payment is considered to be made jointly on behalf of both, given their mutual suretyship. The reasoning clarifies that this does not lead to a vicious cycle (dawr) because equality is established by the half recovery, and both retain full recourse against the original debtor (the principal). The validity of guaranteeing a guarantor is analogically derived (qiyas) from the validity of guaranteeing the principal, as well as from the validity of hawala. The text also notes that this ruling applies regardless of the amount paid (little or much). A key distinction from the previous discussion (the infinite regress case) is that here the mutual guarantee is for the entire amount, and the payment is shared, preventing a cycle. The practical takeaway is that in such arrangements, co-guarantors have a clear right to recover half from each other, and they can also pursue the principal debtor for full reimbursement.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafeel): A guarantor or surety who undertakes to fulfill the obligation of another.
رجوع (ruju'): Recourse; the right of a guarantor to claim reimbursement from the principal debtor or from a co-guarantor after paying the debt.
دور (dawr): A vicious cycle or circular reasoning; a logical fallacy that invalidates an argument.
اصيل (asil): The principal debtor; the person for whom the guarantee is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He cannot recover anything from the co-guarantor.
B) He can recover half from the co-guarantor.
C) He can recover the entire amount from the co-guarantor.
D) Only the principal debtor can be pursued.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, mutual suretyship entitles each guarantor to recover half from the other, and this does not create a vicious cycle because equality is preserved.

Two Guarantors Each Guaranteeing the Other: Ruling and Reasoning
Explains the ruling and reasoning when each of two guarantors is also a guarantor for the other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two guarantors each guarantee the other, explain the qiyas basis, and refute the objection of circularity.

Core Idea
When two guarantors each guarantee the other, the paying guarantor recovers half from his co-guarantor — no circularity arises because equality is achieved.

This lesson explores a nuanced case in Hanafi kafalah: two guarantors standing as sureties for the same debt, with each also guaranteeing the other. The text from al-Hidayah provides the ruling and the qiyas reasoning, addressing a potential objection of infinite regress. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and to identify when an objection is unfounded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and condition
Read the opening line: two men become guarantors for a man for a debt on condition that each is also a guarantor for his companion. Note that each guarantees the full amount from both the principal and the partner.
The condition creates a dual guarantee per person.
2
Extract the ruling
The text states: 'everything that one of them pays, he recovers half from his companion.' This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling applies whether the amount is little or much.
3
Understand the qiyas analogy
The text compares this to the validity of guarantee from the principal (asil) and to hawalah (debt transfer). Each involves a commitment to respond to a claim (iltizam al-mutalabah), which is the effective cause.
The analogy shows that the condition is valid and does not create a novel obligation.
4
Analyze the objection of circularity
Some scholars might argue that allowing recovery from the co-guarantor leads to infinite regress (dawr). The Hanafi response: no circularity because the single recovery (half) establishes equality between the two; a second recovery from the first would break that equality.
Equality is the key principle that stops the regress.
5
Note the final recourse to the principal
After the paying guarantor recovers half from the co-guarantor, both can recover the full amount from the original debtor (asil) because they paid on his behalf.
The principal remains ultimately liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذا كفل رجلان عن رجل بمال على ان كل واحد منهما كفيل عن صاحبه فكل شي اداه احدهما رجع على صاحبه بنصفه قليلا كان او كثيرا ومعنى المسألة في الصحيح ان يكون الكفالة بالكل عن الاصيل وبالكل عن الشريك والمطالبة متعددة فيجتمع الكفالتان على مامر موجبها التزام المطالبة فتصح الكفالة عن الكفيل كما تصح الكفالة عن الاصيل وكما تصح الحوالة من المحتال عليه واذا عرف هذا فما اداه احدهما وقع شائعا عنهما اذ لكل كفالة فلا ترجيح للبعض على البعض بخلاف ماتقدم فيرجع على شريكه بنصفه ولا يؤدي الى الدور لان قضيته الاستواء وقد حصل برجوع احدهما بنصف ما ادى فلا ينقض برجوع الاخر عليه بخلاف ما تقدم ثم يرجعان على الاصيل لانهما اديا عنه احدهما بنفسه والآخر بنائبه وان شاء رجع بالجميع على المكفول عنه لانه كفل بجميع المال عنه بامره
And if two men become guarantors for a man for a debt on condition that each one of them is a guarantor for his companion, then everything that one of them pays, he recovers half from his companion, whether it is little or much. The meaning of the issue, according to the correct view, is that the guarantee is for the whole amount from the principal (original debtor) and for the whole amount from the partner, and the claim is multiple. Thus the two guarantees combine, as has preceded; their effect is to necessitate the claim. So the guarantee from the guarantor is valid just as the guarantee from the principal is valid, and just as the hawala (transfer of debt) from the person against whom the claim is made is valid. And when this is known, whatever one of them pays falls in common between them, because each has a guarantee, so there is no preference of some over others, unlike what preceded. So he recovers half from his partner, and it does not lead to circularity, because its consequence is equality; and equality has been achieved by one of them recovering half of what he paid, so it is not destroyed by the other recovering from him, unlike what preceded. Then both return to the principal, because they paid on his behalf—one directly and the other through his deputy. And if he wishes, he recovers the whole from the person for whom he was guarantor (the principal), because he guaranteed the entire debt on his behalf by his order.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage explains a specific scenario in the book of Kafalah (suretyship). The ruling: When two men become guarantors for a debt owed by a third person, with the condition that each is also a guarantor for the other (i.e., each guarantees the full amount from the original debtor and also guarantees the full amount from his co-guarantor), then if one guarantor pays the entire debt to the creditor, he can recover half of what he paid from his co-guarantor. This is because the payment is considered to have been made jointly on behalf of both guarantors: half from the payer (by virtue of his guarantee from the original debtor) and half from the co-guarantor (by virtue of his guarantee from the paying guarantor). The text emphasizes that this ruling is based on the correct view (al-sahih) and draws an analogy with hawalah (transfer of debt). A key point is that this arrangement does not lead to infinite regress (dawr) because the recovery of half restores equality between the two guarantors, and allowing the second to recover from the first would break that equality. The commentary by the author (Ashraf al-Hadaya) expands on the reasoning, clarifying that each guarantor's obligation arises from two separate guarantees, so the payment is apportioned equally. Finally, both guarantors can then recover the full amount from the original debtor (al-asil), since they paid on his behalf.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of suretyship where one person (kafil) guarantees a debt or obligation of another (asil) to a third party (makful lahu).
كفيل (kafil): The guarantor who undertakes the obligation.
أصيل (asil): The principal debtor whose debt is guaranteed.
مكفول له (makful lahu): The creditor to whom the debt is owed.
دور (dawr): Circularity or infinite regress in recovery of payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire amount he paid
B) Half of what he paid
C) Nothing, because the condition is invalid
D) Only if the co-guarantor agrees

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kafalah, when two guarantors each guarantee the other, the paying guarantor recovers half from his co-guarantor, and the arrangement does not lead to circularity because equality is achieved.

Options for a Co-Surety Who Pays the Full Debt
Explains the options of a co-surety after paying the entire debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two optional recoveries available to a co-surety who pays the entire debt and apply them to a co-suretyship scenario.

Core Idea
A paying co-surety may recover the full amount from the principal or half from the other surety.

When two people jointly guarantee a debt and one ends up paying the entire amount, what are his rights? The classical Hanafi ruling from al-Quduri provides a clear, practical answer. This lesson unpacks that ruling, explaining the reasoning behind the two options and how they operate in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the payment
Recognize that there are two co-sureties (kafeel), a principal debtor (makful 'anhu/aseel), and a creditor (makful lahu). One surety has paid the full debt (e.g., 200 dirhams).
Both sureties are liable for the whole debt, but each is also a surety for the other.
2
State the two options from the matn
Al-Quduri explicitly says the paying surety may either claim the full amount from the principal debtor OR claim half from the other co-surety.
These are alternative, not sequential: he chooses one.
3
Trace the rationale behind each option
Against the principal: because the surety paid on his behalf (by command). Against the co-surety: because each co-surety is a surety for the other's half share.
The commentary expands: paying through a deputy is like paying personally, so both are payers.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Given a modern example (e.g., two guarantors for a $10,000 loan), determine how much the paying guarantor can demand from each party.
The ruling applies regardless of currency or context; the illa (effective cause) is joint suretyship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پھر دونوں کفیل ادا ہوا مال اپنے اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے سکتے ہیں کیونکہ مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے ادا کرنے والے دونوں کفیل ہیں۔ بایں طور کہ ایک نے بذات خود ادا کیا ہے اور دوسرے کفیل نے اپنے نائب کے ذریعہ ادا کیا ہے اور نائب کا ادا کرنا چونکہ ایسا ہے جیسے بذات خود ادا کیا ہو۔ اس لئے گویا ہر ایک نے بذات خود مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے ادا کیا ہے اور جب دونوں کفیلوں نے مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے ادا کیا ہے تو دونوں کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جس کفیل نے مکفول لہ کو دو سو درہم ادا کئے ہیں اس کو جس طرح یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ انصف (ایک سو درہم ) اپنے ساتھی یعنی دوسرے کفیل سے واپس لے اسی طرح یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ وہ پورا مال یعنی دو سو درہم مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے۔ کیونکہ یہ مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے بھی اس کے حکم سے پورے مال کا کفیل ہے۔ لہذا جو کچھ ادا کیا ہے وہ سب مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ایسے دو کفیلوں میں سے ایک کفیل نے اگر مال ادا کیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے مکفول عنہ سے پورا مال واپس لے اور چاہے کفیل سے ادا کردہ کا نصف واپس لے اور پھر دونوں مل کر مکفول عنہ سے واپس لیں ۔
Then both sureties can recover the paid amount from their principal, i.e., the person on whose behalf they stood surety, because both are payers on behalf of the principal. In that one paid personally and the other surety paid through his deputy, and the payment by the deputy is like payment by himself. Therefore it is as if each paid personally on behalf of the principal, and since both sureties paid on behalf of the principal, both will have the right to recourse against the principal. Al-Quduri says: The surety who paid two hundred dirhams to the creditor has the option, just as he can take half (one hundred dirhams) from his partner (the other surety), similarly he can take the entire amount, i.e., two hundred dirhams, from the principal. Because he is also a surety for the entire amount on behalf of the principal by his command. Hence whatever he paid, he can recover it all from the principal. The conclusion is that if one of two such co-sureties pays the debt, he has the option: either to recover the full amount from the principal, or to recover half of what he paid from the co-surety, and then both together recover from the principal.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri regarding two co-sureties who jointly guarantee a debt, each being a surety for the other. The legal issue is: when one surety pays the entire debt, what recourse does he have? The commentary explains that both sureties paid effectively on behalf of the principal, so each can seek reimbursement from him. However, al-Quduri specifies that the paying surety has two options: he may claim the full amount from the principal debtor (makful 'anhu), or he may claim half from his co-surety. The rationale is that the paying surety is a surety for the whole debt on behalf of the principal, so he can directly recover the full amount from him. Alternatively, since both are co-sureties and each is a surety for the other, the paying surety can first recover half from the co-surety, and then both will have recourse against the principal for their respective shares. This ruling is based on the nature of joint surety where each is both a principal (for his own share) and a surety (for the other's share). The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as found in al-Quduri's matn.

Key Terms
کفیل (kafeel): The surety who guarantees the debt of another.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the surety pays.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor who is owed the debt.
اصیل (aseel): The principal debtor himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can only claim half from the co-surety.
B) He can claim the full amount from the principal debtor or claim half from the co-surety.
C) He can only claim from the principal debtor.
D) He cannot claim anything.

Key Takeaway
A co-surety who pays the whole debt has the option to recover the full amount from the principal debtor or half from the other co-surety, reflecting the dual nature of joint suretyship.

Effect of Releasing One Co-Surety
Ruling with talil (reasoning) from al-Hidayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a creditor releases one of two co-sureties and explain the legal reasoning that the principal debtor's obligation remains unaffected.

Core Idea
Releasing one surety does not release the debt – the remaining surety can be held for the whole.

When two people stand surety for the same debt, each guaranteeing the debtor's obligation, what happens if the creditor releases one of them? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer: the other surety remains fully liable. This ruling hinges on the principle that releasing a surety does not release the principal debtor, because the surety's obligation is accessory to the principal's. In this lesson, we will unpack that reasoning and see its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a creditor releasing one of two co-sureties. The ruling is that the creditor may demand the full debt from the other surety.
2
Locate the legal proof (dalil)
The proof is a legal reasoning (talil): because releasing the surety does not necessitate releasing the principal debtor. The principal remains liable, and the other surety is a surety for the entire amount.
No scriptural text is cited; the proof is logical inference from the nature of suretyship.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (the link)
The link is that suretyship is an accessory obligation (tabi'). The surety guarantees the debt of the principal. When the creditor releases one surety, that action only affects that surety's obligation, not the principal's. Since the principal still owes the debt, the other surety (who guaranteed the whole) remains bound.
4
Note any ikhtilaf (disagreement)
There is no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute on this specific point; it is a unanimous ruling within the Hanafi school and generally accepted elsewhere.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
The creditor has the right to pursue the remaining surety for the full debt. The surety cannot argue that his liability is reduced because the other surety was released.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رب المال نے ایک کفیل کو بری کر دیا دوسرے سے پورا مال وصول کر سکتا ہے
قال وإذا أبرأ رب المال احدهما اخذ الأخر بالجميع لان ابراء الكفيل لا يوجب براءة الاصيل فبقى المال كله على الاصيل والأخر كفيل عنه بكله على مابيناه ولهذا ياخذه به
ترجمہ اور اگر رب المال نے دو کفیلوں میں سے ایک کو بری کر دیا تو وہ دوسرے سے پورا مال لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ کفیل کو بری کرنا اصیل کے بری ہونے کو واجب نہیں کرتا ہے۔ پس اصیل پر پورا مال باقی ہے اور دوسرا اس کی طرف سے پورے مال کا کفیل ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اسی وجہ سے مکفول لہ کفیل کو پورے مال میں ماخوذ کر سکتا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب ایک شخص کی طرف سے دو آدمی کفیل ہو گئے اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کی طرف ے کفیل ہے تو ایسے دو کفیلوں میں سے اگر ایک کفیل کو مکفول لہ نے بری کر دیا تو مکفول لہ کو دوسرے کفیل سے پورا قرضہ وصول کرنے کا حق حاصل ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ کفیل کو بری کرنے سے مکفول عنہ بری نہیں ہوتا اور جب مکفول عنہ بری نہیں ہوا تو اس پر پورا قرضہ باقی رہا۔ اور دوسرا کفیل اس کی طرف سے پورے قرضہ کا کفیل ہے جیسا کہ پہلے گذر چکا۔ اور چونکہ مکفول عنہ پر پورا قرضہ باقی ہے اور دوسرا اس کی طرف سے پورے قرضہ کا کفیل ہے۔ اس لئے مکفول لہ اس کفیل سے جو قرضہ کے مطالبہ سے بری نہیں ہوا پورے قرضہ کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔
If the creditor releases one of them, he can take the whole [debt] from the other. Because releasing the surety does not necessitate the release of the principal; thus the entire debt remains on the principal, and the other [surety] is a surety for him for the whole, as we have explained. For this reason, the creditor can hold the surety for the whole debt.
Commentary: The scenario is that two men stood surety for one person, and each of them is a surety for the other. If the creditor releases one of them, the creditor has the right to recover the entire debt from the other surety. Because releasing a surety does not release the principal, and when the principal is not released, the entire debt remains on him, and the other surety is a surety for the entire debt on his behalf, as was previously explained. Since the entire debt remains on the principal and the other is surety for it, the creditor can demand the full debt from that surety who was not released from the demand.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: if a creditor releases one of two co-sureties (each being a surety for the other), the other surety remains liable for the entire debt. The reasoning is that releasing a surety does not release the principal debtor (makful 'anhu). The principal's obligation remains, and the unreleased surety is a surety for the entire amount on his behalf. Therefore, the creditor can demand the full debt from the remaining surety. This is because the surety contract is an accessory obligation; discharging one surety does not affect the principal debt or the other surety's guarantee. The ruling is from the matn (Quduri) and is explained in the commentary. Authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra): Release or discharge from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor releases one of two co-sureties, what is the liability of the other surety?
A) He is released as well.
B) He is liable for only half the debt.
C) He is liable for the entire debt.
D) He can choose whether to pay or not.

Key Takeaway
Releasing one co-surety does not affect the principal debt; the remaining surety remains liable for the entire amount.

Joint Kitabah with Mutual Suretyship
Ruling on joint kitabah with mutual suretyship, justified by istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on joint kitabah with mutual suretyship and explain why it is valid by istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Joint kitabah with mutual suretyship is permitted by istihsan despite potential qiyas objections.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in kitabah (contract of manumission by payment) where two slaves enter into a single joint contract and each stands as a surety for the other. Strict analogy (qiyas) might forbid such a suretyship due to uncertainty, but Hanafi jurists employ istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it, treating each slave as a principal (asil) for his own share of the obligation. Understanding this ruling illustrates the importance of istihsan as a formal source of Hanafi law and its role in achieving equitable outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The act is two slaves being made mukatib jointly with mutual suretyship. The ruling is that the contract is permissible (sahih) by istihsan.
The passage states 'kafalat istihsanan ja'iz' (the suretyship is permissible by istihsan).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The proof is not a text but istihsan itself. In Hanafi usul, istihsan is a valid source that can override qiyas. The passage uses 'istihsanan' to indicate this method.
Istihsan is based on considerations of public interest and removal of hardship.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does istihsan prove the ruling? The method is to treat each slave as a principal (asil) regarding his own portion of the obligation. Thus, the suretyship is for the other's share, not an uncertain guarantee.
This avoids the qiyas objection that mutual suretyship involves gharar (uncertainty).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may reject this using qiyas, arguing that suretyship with unknown obligation is invalid. The Hanafi position openly departs from qiyas via istihsan.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in methodological differences.
5
Determine the thamarah
What is the practical consequence? If one slave pays the entire kitabah amount, he can recover half from the other slave. This is stated in the passage.
Each slave is liable for his own half; the suretyship ensures the master can collect from either.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو غلام ایک ہی بدل کتابت پر مکاتب بنائے گئے اور ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی طرف سے مولی کے لئے کفیل ہو گیا تو کفالت استحسانا جائز ہے
قال وإذا كوتب العبد ان كتابة واحدة وكل واحد منهما كفيل عن صاحبه فكل شي اداه احدهما رجع على صاحبه بنصفه ووجهه ان هذا العقد جائز استحسانا وطريقه ان يجعل كل واحد منهما اصيلا في حق وجوب
Two slaves were made mukatib (contract for freedom) with one single kitabah payment, and each became a surety for the other to the master. Then the suretyship is permissible by istihsan.
He said: If two slaves are made mukatib with one kitabah, and each is a surety for his partner, then whatever one pays, he can recourse against his partner for half. The explanation is that this contract is permissible by istihsan, and its method is to consider each of them as a principal regarding the obligation...
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario in kitabah (contract of manumission by payment). Two slaves enter into a single kitabah contract with their master, and each slave stands as a surety for the other. The ruling is that such a suretyship is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), even though qiyas might forbid it due to the uncertainty or potential for injustice. The method of istihsan is to treat each slave as a principal (aseel) in respect of the obligation, meaning each is directly responsible for his share, and the suretyship is for the other's share. Therefore, if one slave pays the entire kitabah amount, he can recover half from his co-slave. The text is incomplete but provides the core ruling that this arrangement is permissible under Hanafi fiqh. Authority weight: This appears to be from the matn (possibly al-Quduri or similar), so likely Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to earn his freedom by paying installments.
کتابت (kitabah): A contract between master and slave for the slave's freedom in exchange for a specified payment.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to deviate from strict qiyas for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas
B) Istihsan
C) Ijma
D) Textual evidence from Quran

Key Takeaway
Joint kitabah with mutual suretyship is valid by istihsan, and each slave can recover half from the other if he pays the full amount.

Creditors' Right to Full Debt After Muwafada Dissolution
Ruling with proof on creditors' right after dissolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that after dissolution of a muwafada partnership, creditors may claim the full debt from either former partner, and identify the basis in mutual guarantee (kafalah).

Core Idea
After muwafada dissolves, creditors may claim the full debt from either partner—the guarantee persists.

The dissolution of a muwafada partnership does not extinguish the mutual guarantee that existed during the partnership. This lesson examines the creditors' right to claim the entire debt from either former partner, based on the principle that each partner remains a guarantor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Partners have dissolved a muwafada (equal partnership) but debts remain from the partnership period.
Dissolution does not erase pre-existing obligations.
2
State the ruling
Creditors have the right to take the entire debt from whichever of the two former partners they choose.
The creditor's choice is unrestricted; he can claim 100% from either.
3
Understand the reason (talil)
Each partner is a guarantor (kafil) for the other during the partnership, and this guarantee continues after dissolution for debts incurred during the partnership.
The basis is the mutual agency and guarantee inherent in muwafada.
4
Recognize the limit
The paying partner may later seek recourse from the other only for the amount exceeding half of the debt (covered in next lesson).
This limitation does not affect the creditor's immediate right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور جب متفاوضین (اپنی شرکت سے ) جدا ہو گئے تو قرض خواہوں کو اختیار ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے جس سے چاہیں پورا قرضہ وصول کریں کیونکہ متفاوفین میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی طرف سے كفیل ہے جیسا کہ کتاب الشرکۃ میں معلوم ہو چکا۔ اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک اپنے ساتھی سے رجوع نہ کر ھے یہاں تک کہ نصف سے زائد ادا کر دے اُن دو دلیلوں کی وجہ سے جو کفالۃ الرجلین میں گذر چکی ہیں۔
تشریح مفاوضہ ایسی تجارت ہے جس میں دو آدمی شریک ہوں اور دونوں بال آزادی عقل اور دین کے اعتبار سے مساوی اور برابر ہوں ۔ شرکت مفاوضہ وکالت اور كفالت دونوں کو متضمن ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی شریکین میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کی طرف سے وکیل بھی ہوتا ہے اور نفیل بھی ہوتا ہے۔ مفاوضہ، تفویض سے مشتق ہے اور تفویض کے معنی سپرد کرنے کے ہیں اور شریکین میں سے ہر ایک چونکہ تصرف کو اپنے ساتھی کے سپر د کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کا نام مفاوضہ رکھا گیا۔
صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر متفاوفین نے شرکت مفاوضہ کو ختم کر دیا اور اُن پر لوگوں کا قرضہ ہو تو قرض خواہوں کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنا پورا قرضہ ان دونوں میں سے جس سے چاہیں وصول کریں کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک عقد مفاوضہ کی وجہ سے اپنے شریک کی طرف سے نفیل ہے پس ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر نصف قرضہ بحق اصالت واجب ہوگا اور نصف قرضہ بحق کفالت واجب ہوگا۔ بہر حال ہر ایک پر پورا قرضہ لازم ہے۔ اور جب ہر ایک پر پورا قرضہ لازم ہے تو ہر ایک سے پورا قرضہ وصول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر قرض خواہوں نے اُن دونوں میں سے ایک سے مطالبہ کر کے قرضہ لے لیا تو اس کو اپنے ساتھی سے واپس لینے کا اختیار اس وقت ہوگا جب نصف قرضہ سے زائد ادا کر دے۔ چنانچہ نصف قرضہ ادا کرنے کی صورت میں اپنے ساتھی سے قطعا رجوع نہ کرے۔ اور نصف سے زائد ادا کرنے کی صورت میں صرف مقدار زائد واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ اس پر كفالۃ الرجلین کے پہلے مسئلہ میں دو دلیلیں گذر چکی ہیں ملاحظہ فرمالیں۔
He said: And when the two muwafada partners separate, creditors have the right to take from whichever of them they wish the entire debt, because each of them is a guarantor for his partner as known in the partnership, and one of them does not recourse against his partner until he pays more than half, due to the two arguments mentioned in the kafalah of two men.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage states a ruling for when the parties to a muwafada (equal partnership) dissolve their partnership. The creditors retain the right to claim the full debt from either former partner, because each partner is a guarantor for the other during the partnership, and that guarantor obligation continues after dissolution. However, if one partner pays the full debt, he can only claim recourse from the other partner for the amount exceeding half. If he pays exactly half, he cannot recourse at all. This is based on two proofs explained earlier in the section on kafalah of two men (kafalat al-rajulayn). The commentary explains that muwafada includes both agency and guarantee, and the ruling ensures that creditors are not disadvantaged by the dissolution.

Key Terms
مفاوضہ (muwafada): An equal partnership where partners are equal in freedom, reason, and religion, and each is both agent and guarantor for the other.
کفیل (kafil): A guarantor who is responsible for the debt of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After dissolution of a muwafada partnership, a creditor can claim the full debt from:
A) Both partners together, each paying half.
B) Either partner, at the creditor's choice.
C) Only the partner who incurred the debt.
D) Neither, because dissolution ends liability.

Key Takeaway
Dissolution of muwafada does not terminate the mutual guarantee; creditors can claim the full debt from either former partner.

Recourse Limitation Between Former Muwafada Partners
Condition for recourse after muwafada dissolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a paying partner can only recover the amount exceeding half of the debt from his former partner, and apply the rule to specific amounts.

Core Idea
Each partner bears half as principal and half as guarantor; paying more than half allows recourse for the excess.

While creditors have broad rights, the internal recourse between former partners is restricted. This lesson focuses on the rule that the paying partner cannot recourse for half; he can only claim the excess over half. This is based on the dual liability of each partner: half as principal (asil) and half as guarantor (kafil).

Guided Path
1
Understand dual liability
In muwafada, each partner is liable for half the debt as principal (since debts are shared equally) and for the other half as guarantor for the partner.
The half as principal is his own obligation; the half as guarantor is secondary.
2
State the recourse rule
A paying partner cannot recourse against the other until he pays more than half of the total debt.
If he pays exactly half, he has only paid his own share; no right to recover from the other.
3
Apply the rule
If he pays more than half, he can recover only the excess over half from the other partner.
Example: Total debt 1000; partner pays 700. He can recover 200 from the other (700-500).
4
Reference the proof
The text refers to two arguments from the section on kafalah of two men (kafalat al-rajulayn) that establish this limitation.
The proofs are not reproduced here but are assumed from earlier study.

Mutual Kafalah of Mukatabs: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on mutual kafalah of two mukatabs in one contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to validate a mutual kafalah between two mukatab slaves in a single kitabah contract and distinguish it from the invalid case of separate contracts.

Core Idea
Two mukatabs in one contract: mutual kafalah valid by istihsan, not qiyas.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario from al-Hidayah where the Hanafi school departs from strict analogy (qiyas) using istihsan to uphold the objective of the kitabah contract. The case involves a master making two slaves mukatib under a single contract with mutual guarantees. While other schools deem this invalid, Hanafis validate it by reinterpreting each slave as a principal debtor. Understanding this ruling illuminates how Hanafi jurists prioritize legal facilitation over rigid analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the mutual kafalah is valid (jā'iz) by istihsan. Note the result: each slave who pays recovers half from the other.
The ruling applies only when the kitabah contract is a single transaction.
2
Identify the opposing view and their proof
Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad hold it invalid by qiyas. Their basis: a mukatab cannot be a guarantor (kafalah is a gratuitous act, and a mukatab lacks full ownership for gratuitous transfers) and the kitabah debt is not a valid debt for kafalah.
The qiyas argument relies on the general principles of kafalah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response based on istihsan
The Hanafi response reinterprets the arrangement: each slave is treated as a principal (asīl) for the full amount, so his freedom is conditional on his payment. The guarantee is incidental; the contract is seen as a conditional manumission, not a true kafalah.
The key is that the kitabah contract is single, so the obligation is shared.
4
Contrast with separate kitabah contracts
If the two slaves were made mukatib individually (separate contracts), even the Hanafi school would hold the mutual kafalah invalid by both qiyas and istihsan. This boundary clarifies the scope of the exception.
In separate contracts, each slave is a true guarantor for the other's debt, which is impermissible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, Hanafi courts enforce the guarantee and allow recourse for half. In non-Hanafi jurisdictions, such a guarantee may be rejected if the master tries to enforce it directly.
The dispute has real-world implications for enforcement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإذا كوتب العبد ان كتابة واحدة وكل واحد منهما كفيل عن صاحبه فكل شي اداه احدهما رجع على صاحبه بنصفه ووجهه ان هذا العقد جائز استحسانا وطريقه ان يجعل كل واحد منهما اصيلا في حق وجوب الالف عليه فيكون عتقهما معلقابا دائه ويجعل كفيلا بالالف فى حق صاحبه وسنذكره في المكاتب ان شاء الله تعالى واذا عرف ذلك فما اداه احدهما رجع بنصفه على صاحبه لاستوائهما ولو رجع بالكل لا تتحقق المساواة

اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ كفالہ کی اس صورت کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے یہ کہا جائے گا کہ دونوں غلاموں میں سے ہر ایک پر ایک ہزار کا وجوب اصالہ ہے نہ کہ كفالہ اور دونوں کی آزادی ایک ہزار ادا کرنے پر معلق ہے۔ گویا مولی نے دونوں غلاموں میں سے ہر ایک سے یوں کہا کہ اگر تو نے ایک ہزار درہم ادا کر دئیے تو تم دونوں آزاد ہو۔ پس دونوں میں سے جو بھی ایک ہزار ادا کرے گا اُس کے ادا کرنے سے دونوں غلام آزاد ہو جائیں گے ۔ اور مولی دونوں میں سے ہر ایک سے جمیع مال یعنی ایک ہزار کا مطالبہ بحکم اصالت کرے گا نہ کہ بحکم كفالت ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ یہ ایک ہزار درہم ، بدل کتابت نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ ایک ہزار کی ادائیگی پر آزادی کو معلق کرنا ہے۔ اور مال ادا کرنے پر آزادی کو معلق کرنے اور مکاتبت کے درمیان فرق ہے۔ جیسا کہ باب العتق علی جعل ج ۲ میں یہ بحث گذر بھی چکی ہے اور مزید تف ید تفصیل
He said: And if the two slaves are made mukatib by one kitabah contract and each of them is a guarantor for his partner, then whatever one of them pays, he recourses against his partner for half of it. The reasoning is that this contract is valid by istihsan, and the method is that each of them is made a principal regarding the obligation of the thousand upon him, so their manumission is conditional upon his payment, and he is made a guarantor for the thousand regarding his partner. We will mention it in the chapter on mukatab, God willing. And when that is known, what one of them pays, he recourses for half against his partner because of their equality; if he recoups the whole, equality is not realized.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific case: a master makes his two slaves mukatib (contractually bound for their freedom) under a single kitabah contract, and each slave becomes a guarantor (kafil) for the other to the master. According to the Hanafi school, this mutual kafalah is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), but it would be invalid by qiyas (analogy). The basis for istihsan is that each slave is treated as a principal (asil) for the full amount (here 1000 dirhams), so his freedom is conditional on paying that amount; the guarantee element is thus reinterpreted. If the contract were separate (each slave mukatib individually), the kafalah would be invalid even by istihsan because a mukatib cannot validly be a guarantor (kafalah is a gratuitous act, and a mukatib does not have full ownership over gratuities). The passage also notes that Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad hold the kafalah invalid by qiyas. The Hanafi position relies on structuring the contract as a conditional manumission rather than a true kafalah.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master for his freedom in exchange for a specified payment.
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of guarantee where one person (the kafil) becomes surety for another's debt or obligation.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, such as necessity or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the mutual kafalah of two mukatab slaves in one contract valid by istihsan?
A) Because a mukatab has full ownership rights.
B) Because each slave is treated as a principal for the full amount, making freedom conditional on payment.
C) Because the master waived the right to object.
D) Because the debt is considered a proper debt for kafalah.

Key Takeaway
When two slaves are jointly mukatab in one contract, mutual kafalah is valid by Hanafi istihsan because each is a principal debtor, not a true guarantor.
